### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Allen starts from point X and goes to point Y.
  - Bob starts from point Y and goes towards point X.
  - Once Allen reaches point Y he changes his direction and returns to point X.
  - Once Bob reaches point X, he changes his direction and returns to point Y.
  - Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78 kmph.
  - By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen.
Thought:
  - Let the distance between point X and point Y be d km.
  - Let t1 be the time taken for Allen to reach point Y for the first time.
  - Let t2 be the time taken for Allen to reach point X for the second time.
  - Let t3 be the time taken for Bob to reach point X for the first time.
  - Let t4 be the time taken for Bob to reach point Y for the second time.
  - From the given information, we know that:
    - Allen's speed = 54 kmph
    - Bob's speed = 78 kmph
    - Distance covered by Allen in t1 hours = d/2 km
    - Distance covered by Bob in t1 hours = d/2 km
    - Distance covered by Allen in t2 hours = d km
    - Distance covered by Bob in t3 hours = 78t3 km
    - Distance covered by Bob in t4 hours = 78t4 km
    - Distance covered by Allen in t4 hours = 54t4 km
    - Distance covered by Bob in t4 hours - Distance covered by Allen in t4 hours = 48 km
  - We can write the following equations:
    - d/2 + 78t3 = d - 54t4  (Equation 1)
    - 78t3 - 78t4 = 48        (Equation 2)
    - Solving Equation 2, we get t3 - t4 = 48/78
    - Substituting t3 - t4 = 48/78 in Equation 1, we get:
      d/2 + 78(t3 - 48/78) = d - 54t4
      Simplifying, we get:
      d = 126 km
  - Therefore, the distance between point X and point Y is 126 km.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Allen starts from X and goes to Y, and Bob starts from Y and goes to X.
  Once they meet, Allen changes his direction and returns to X while Bob changes his direction and returns to Y.
  Allen travels at 54kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph.
  Bob covers 48km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
Thought: 
  Let the distance between X and Y be d km.
  Let t1 be the time it takes for Allen to reach Y.
  Let t2 be the time it takes for Bob to reach X.
  Let t3 be the time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time.
  Let t4 be the time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the second time.
  Since Allen and Bob meet at some point between X and Y, let the distance from X to the point where they meet be x km.
  Then, the distance from the point where they meet to Y is (d - x) km.
  In the first t1 hours, Allen covers xt1 km, and in the same t1 hours, Bob covers (d - x)t1 km.
  Therefore, xt1 + (d - x)t1 = d, which simplifies to t1 = d/(54+78) hours.
  In the same t1 hours, Bob covers (d - x)t1 km.
  Therefore, x = 78t1.
  Similarly, in the first t2 hours, Bob covers (d - xt2) km, and in the same t2 hours, Allen covers x t2 km.
  Therefore, (d - x)t2 + xt2 = d, which simplifies to t2 = d/(54+78) hours.
  In the same t2 hours, Allen covers xt2 km.
  Therefore, d - x = 54t2.
  In the first t3 hours, Allen covers 54t3 km, and in the same t3 hours, Bob covers 78t3 km.
  Therefore, 54t3 + 78t3 = d, which simplifies to t3 = d/(54+78) hours.
  In the first t4 hours, Allen covers 54t4 km, and in the same t4 hours, Bob covers 78t4 km.
  Therefore, 54t4 + 78t4 - 48 = d, since Bob covers 48 km more than Allen.
  Simplifying, we get 132t4 = d + 48.
  Substituting t4 = d/(54+78), we get 132d/(54+78) = d + 48.
  Solving for d, we get d = 126 km.
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 126 km.

  - Relative speed = Sum of speeds of the two objects

  Let the time taken by Allen to reach Y be t hours.
  At that time, Bob has traveled (54 + 78)t = 132t km.
  Let the time taken by Allen to return to X be u hours.
  At that time, Bob has traveled (54 + 78)(t + u) = 132(t + u) km.

  Total distance traveled by Allen = d km + d km = 2d km.
  Bob covers 48 km more than Allen during this time, so we can write:
  2 * 132(t + u) - 2d = 48.

  264(t + u) - 2d = 48.

  Distance = Speed x Time
  So, we can write:
  d = 54t + 78u (distance traveled by Allen)
  d = 78t + 54u (distance traveled by Bob)
  Solving these equations simultaneously, we get:
  t = d/72
  u = d/126
  Substituting these values in the equation 264(t + u) - 2d = 48, we get:
  264(d/72 + d/126) - 2d = 48
  Simplifying, we get:
  d = 126 km
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 126 km.

  During the return journey, the speed of the jeep increased by 12km/hr.
  The speed of the jeep in the return journey is S+12.
  The time taken for the return journey is 4 hours.

  Distance travelled in the forward journey = S x 6  = 6S.
  Distance travelled in the return journey = (S+12) x 4 = 4S + 48.
  The total distance travelled by the jeep = Distance travelled in the forward journey + Distance travelled in the return journey.
  Total distance travelled = 6S + 4S + 48 = 10S + 48.
  We need to find the value of S to calculate the total distance travelled.
  During the forward journey, the distance travelled is D = 6S.
  During the return journey, the distance travelled is D = 4(S+12) = 4S + 48.
  Equating both the distances, we get 6S = 4S + 48.
  Solving for S, we get S = 24.
  Therefore, the total distance travelled = 10S + 48 = 10(24) + 48 = 240 + 48 = 288km.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  If there is one water lily on the first day, then on the second day there will be two, on the fourth day there will be four, on the sixth day there will be eight, and so on.
Thought:
  If there is one water lily on the first day and it takes 60 days to cover the lake, then the number of doublings that occur is 60/2 = 30.
  Therefore, there will be 2^30 water lilies on the lake after 60 days.
  If there are initially 64 water lilies, then we need to find out how many doublings are required to get to 2^30 from 64.
  2^6 = 64, so we only need 24 doublings to get to 2^30 from 64.
  Since each doubling takes two days, it will take 24*2 = 48 days to get from 64 to 2^30.
  Adding this to the initial day when there were already 64 water lilies, the lake will be fully covered with lilies in 48+1 = 49 days.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 53.
Criticism:
  There is a mistake in the calculation. 
  2^6 is equal to 64, so we need 24 doublings to get from 64 to 2^30.
  However, this will take 24*2 = 48 days, not 53.
  Therefore, the correct answer is not D: 53, but E: 59.
Action: Answer("E")

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The distance between City A and City B is the same for both trains.
  Train M takes 4 hours to travel from City A to City B.
  Train N takes 3 hours and 30 minutes to travel from City B to City A.
  The total time between Train M's departure and Train N's arrival is 8 hours and 30 minutes.
Thought:
  Train M travels for 4 hours before Train N starts moving.
  In those 4 hours, Train M covers a distance of 4x, where x is the speed of Train M.
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours after Train M arrives in City B.
  In those 3.5 hours, Train N covers a distance of 3.5y, where y is the speed of Train N.
  The total distance between City A and City B is 4x+3.5y.
  When the two trains meet, they will have covered the entire distance between City A and City B.
  Let's assume that Train M and Train N meet after t hours from 7 am (when Train N starts moving).
  Then, Train M will have traveled for (t+2) hours and Train N will have traveled for (t-1) hours.
  The distance covered by Train M in (t+2) hours is (t+2)x.
  The distance covered by Train N in (t-1) hours is (t-1)y.
  Therefore, (t+2)x + (t-1)y = 4x + 3.5y.
  Solving for t, we get t = 55/60 hours = 55 minutes.
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other at 7:55 am.
  The answer is E: 55 min.
Criticism:
  There is no criticism to this solution.

  Distance traveled by Train M = Speed of Train M x Time taken = S × t
  Distance traveled by Train N = Speed of Train N x Time taken = S × (t-2)
  Total distance traveled by both trains = Distance traveled by Train M + Distance traveled by Train N
  Therefore, S × t + S × (t-2) = D
  where D is the distance between City A and City B.

  We also know that Train N takes 3.5 hours to travel from B to A, so its speed is D/3.5.

  Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am, which means it takes 4 hours to reach City B.
  Train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 10:30am, which means it takes 3.5 hours to reach City A.
Thought:
  Let's assume that the two trains cross each other after x hours from the time Train N left City B.
  The distance traveled by Train M in x hours will be (4 - x) hours.
  The distance traveled by Train N in x hours will be 3.5 hours.
  Since both trains travel the same distance when they meet, we can set up the following equation:
  Distance traveled by Train M = Distance traveled by Train N
  Speed of Train M * Time taken by Train M = Speed of Train N * Time taken by Train N
  Let's assume that the speed of Train M is S1 and the speed of Train N is S2.
  Therefore, the equation becomes:
  S1 * (4 - x) = S2 * 3.5
  We know that Train N leaves City B at 7 am, which means it has been traveling for (x + 2) hours when the two trains meet.
  Therefore, the equation becomes:
  S1 * (4 - x) = S2 * (x + 2)
  We also know that the total distance between the two cities is the same, which means:
  S1 * 4 = S2 * 3.5
  We can solve these two equations to find x:
  S1 * (4 - x) = (S1 * 4 * (x + 2)) / 3.5
  14S1 - 3.5S1x = 16S1x + 8S1
  11.5S1x = 8S1
  x = 8 / 11.5 ≈ 0.7

  7:42 am

Response 6:
Knowledge: 
  Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am. Therefore, the time taken by train M is 4 hours.
  Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am. Therefore, the time taken by train N is 3.5 hours.
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the two trains meet after x hours from 7am (when train N started).
  Therefore, train M travels for (x+2) hours (since it started at 5am) before it meets train N.
  Distance traveled by train M = speed of train M x time = SM(x+2), where SM is the speed of train M.
  Distance traveled by train N = speed of train N x time = SN(x), where SN is the speed of train N.
  Since the two trains meet each other, the total distance traveled by them is the same. Therefore, SM(x+2) = SN(x).
  Solving for x, we get x = (14/3) hours = 4 hours 40 minutes.
  Therefore, the two trains meet each other 4 hours 40 minutes after 7am, which is at 11:40am.
  Therefore, the time taken for the two trains to cross each other is 4 hours 40 minutes - 3.5 hours = 1 hour 10 minutes.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 1 hr 15 min.

Response 7:
Knowledge:
  Train M takes 4 hours to travel from City A to City B.
  Train N takes 3.5 hours to travel from City B to City A.
  The two trains are moving towards each other.
Thought:
  Let's assume that the two trains meet after x hours.
  Train M has traveled for x hours and Train N has traveled for (x - 2) hours.
  The total distance covered by both trains is equal to the distance between City A and City B.
  The distance covered by Train M = speed of Train M * time taken = x * SM
  The distance covered by Train N = speed of Train N * time taken = (x - 2) * SN
  Here, SM and SN are the speeds of Train M and Train N respectively.
  As the two trains meet, the total distance covered by both the trains is equal to the distance between City A and City B.
  Therefore, x * SM + (x - 2) * SN = distance between City A and City B
  We know that SM = distance between City A and City B / 4 and SN = distance between City A and City B / 3.5
  Substituting these values in the above equation, we get:
  x * (distance between City A and City B / 4) + (x - 2) * (distance between City A and City B / 3.5) = distance between City A and City B
  Solving for x, we get x = 14/9 hours = 1 hour 33 minutes.
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other 1 hour and 33 minutes after Train M leaves City A, which is at 6:33 am.
  To get the time when the two trains cross each other, we add 1 hour 33 minutes to 5:00 am, which gives us 6:33 am + 1 hour 33 minutes = 8:06 am.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 1 hr 23 min.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 84 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The formula for the arithmetic mean is: sum of values / number of values.
  Let's call the sum of the weights of the 10 vehicles "S" and the weight of the new truck "x".
  We know that the average weight of the 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons, so: S/10 = 12.2.
  We also know that the average weight increased by 2.6 tons after the new truck was added, so: (S+x)/11 = 14.8.
Thought: 
  We have two equations with two unknowns:
  S/10 = 12.2  --> S = 122
  (S+x)/11 = 14.8  --> S+x = 162.8
  Substituting S from the first equation into the second equation, we get:
  122 + x = 162.8
  x = 40.8
  Therefore, the weight of the new truck is 40.8 tons.
  The answer is A: 40.8.
Criticism: 
  Your thought process and calculations are correct.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The formula for the arithmetic mean is: sum of all values / number of values.
  We know the average weight of the 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons.
  We know that the average weight increased by 2.6 tons after adding a new heavy duty truck.
Thought: 
  Let's call the weight of the new truck "x".
  The sum of the weights of the original 10 vehicles is 10 * 12.2 = 122 tons.
  After adding the new truck, the sum of the weights of all 11 vehicles is (10 * 12.2) + x.
  We know that the new average weight is 12.2 + 2.6 = 14.8 tons.
  Therefore, we can set up the following equation:
  (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  Solving for x:
  122 + x = 11 * 14.8
  122 + x = 162.8
  x = 40.8
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 40.8 tons.
  The answer is A: 40.8.
Criticism: 
  Your solution is correct.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The average (arithmetic mean) of a set of n numbers is the sum of the numbers divided by n.
  If the average of a set of n numbers is increased by x, then the sum of the numbers is increased by nx.
Thought:
  Let the weight of the new truck be x.
  The total weight of the 10 vehicles before the new truck was added is 10 * 12.2 = 122 tons.
  After the new truck was added, the total weight of the 11 vehicles is (10 * 12.2) + x = 122 + x.
  The average weight of the 11 vehicles is (122 + x) / 11.
  The average weight increased by 2.6 tons, so (122 + x) / 11 = 12.2 + 2.6.
  Solving for x, we get x = 41.6.
  Therefore, the weight in tons of the heavy-duty truck is 41.6.

  After the new truck was added, there are 11 vehicles in the group.
  The new total weight of the group is (10 * 12.2) + x.

  (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  Multiplying both sides by 11:
  122 + x = 162.8
  Subtracting 122 from both sides:
  x = 40.8
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 40.8 tons.

Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The current mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay.
  We need to remove and replace some of the mixture to make it contain equal quantities of sand and clay.
Thought: 
  Let's assume we have 10kg of the mixture. 
  The amount of sand in the mixture is 30% of 10kg = 3kg.
  The amount of clay in the mixture is 70% of 10kg = 7kg.
  To make the mixture contain equal quantities of sand and clay, we need to add 4kg of sand to the mixture.
  We need to remove some of the mixture to make room for the additional sand.
  Let's assume we remove x kg of the mixture.
  The amount of sand in the remaining mixture is still 3kg, but it is now 50% of the mixture.
  We add 4kg of sand to the remaining mixture, so the total amount of sand is 3kg + 4kg = 7kg.
  The total amount of mixture after adding the sand is still 10kg.
  The amount of clay in the remaining mixture is 10kg - 7kg = 3kg.
  The amount of clay in the remaining mixture is also 50% of the mixture.
  Since we removed x kg of the mixture, the amount of clay in the removed mixture was 70% of x kg = 0.7x.
  We replaced the removed mixture with pure sand, so the amount of clay in the added sand is 0.
  The amount of clay in the final mixture is 50% of 10kg = 5kg.
  Therefore, the amount of clay in the remaining mixture is 3kg, and the amount of clay in the added sand is 0.
  The total amount of clay removed from the mixture is 7kg - 5kg = 2kg.
  The amount of clay in the removed mixture is 0.7x.
  Therefore, 0.7x = 2kg.
  Solving for x, we get: x = 20/7 kg.
  Therefore, we need to remove 20/7 kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
  Answer: B) 20/7

  In order to have equal quantities of sand and clay, we need to have 5 kg of sand and 5 kg of clay.
  This means we need to remove 3 kg of sand and replace it with 2 kg of sand.
  To calculate how much of the mixture needs to be removed, we can use the formula:
  amount removed = (initial amount of sand - desired amount of sand) / (total amount of mixture - desired amount of sand)
  amount removed = (3 - 2) / (10 - 5)
  amount removed = 1/5
  This means we need to remove 1/5 of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
  To calculate the amount of mixture to be removed, we can use the formula:
  amount of mixture removed = (1/5) * 10
  amount of mixture removed = 2 kg
  Therefore, we need to remove 2 kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.

Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all four sides of the rectangle.
  The cost of gardening a rectangular plot depends on the area of the plot and the rate per square meter.
Thought:
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular plot is L and the width is W.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is given as 2(L+W) = 340 m.
  Therefore, L+W = 170 m.
  We need to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The length of the outer boundary of the rectangular plot will be (L+2) and the width will be (W+2).
  The area of the boundary will be (L+2)(W+2) - LW.
  Simplifying this expression, we get 2L + 2W + 4 = 2(L+W) + 4 = 2(170) + 4 = 344.
  Therefore, the area of the boundary is 344 square meters.
  The cost of gardening the boundary at the rate of 10 per square meter will be 344 * 10 = 3440.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 3440.
Criticism: 
  There is no error in the solution.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(length + width)
  We are given the perimeter of the rectangular plot.
  We need to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter wide boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The cost will be the product of the area of the boundary and the rate per square meter.
Thought:
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular plot is L and the width is W.
  Perimeter of the rectangular plot = 2(L + W) = 340
  L + W = 170
  We need to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter wide boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The length of the rectangular plot with the boundary = L + 2
  The width of the rectangular plot with the boundary = W + 2
  Area of the rectangular plot with the boundary = (L + 2) * (W + 2)
  Area of the rectangular plot = L * W
  Area of the boundary = (L + 2) * (W + 2) - L * W
  Area of the boundary = LW + 2L + 2W + 4 - LW
  Area of the boundary = 2L + 2W + 4
  Cost of gardening 1 square meter = 10
  Cost of gardening the boundary = Area of the boundary * Cost of gardening 1 square meter
  Cost of gardening the boundary = (2L + 2W + 4) * 10
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 20L + 20W + 40
  Substituting L + W = 170, we get:
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 20(170 - W) + 20W + 40
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 3400 - 20W + 20W + 40
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 3440
  Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre is 3440.

  On solving the above equations, we get l = 84 and b = 86.
  Therefore, the area of the garden is (84+2)*(86+2) - 84*86 = 3440 square meters.
  The cost of gardening is given as 10 per square meter.
  Therefore, the total cost of gardening the 1-metre broad boundary around the rectangular plot will be 3440*10 = 34400.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 3440.
Criticism: 
  There is no apparent flaw in the above solution.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 7:
Knowledge: 
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2 * (length + breadth)
  To find the cost of gardening, we need to find the area of the rectangular plot plus the area of the 1-metre boundary around it.
Thought: 
  Let's assume the length of the rectangular plot is L and the breadth is B.
  Perimeter of the rectangular plot = 2 * (L + B) = 340
  L + B = 170
  We need to find the cost of gardening the 1-metre broad boundary around the rectangular plot. 
  The length of the outer boundary = L + 2 + B + 2 = L + B + 4
  The breadth of the outer boundary = B + 2 + L + 2 = L + B + 4
  Area of the outer boundary = (L + B + 4) * (L + B + 4) - L * B
  Cost of gardening the outer boundary = Area of the outer boundary * 10
  Cost of gardening the outer boundary = [(L + B + 4) * (L + B + 4) - L * B] * 10
  Cost of gardening the outer boundary = [(L + B)^2 + 8(L + B) + 16 - L * B] * 10
  Cost of gardening the outer boundary = [(170)^2 + 8(170) + 16 - L * B] * 10
  Area of the rectangular plot = L * B
  Total cost of gardening = Cost of gardening the outer boundary + Area of the rectangular plot * 10
  Total cost of gardening = [(170)^2 + 8(170) + 16 - L * B] * 10 + L * B * 10
  Total cost of gardening = 289000 - 10LB

  There is no flaw in the logic or calculations.

Response 9:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(length + breadth)
  We have the perimeter of the rectangular plot, which is 340 meters.
  Let's assume the length of the rectangular plot to be L and the breadth to be B.
  We need to find the cost of gardening 1-metre wide boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The cost of gardening is given as 10 per square metre.
Thought:
  Perimeter of the rectangular plot = 2(L + B) = 340 meters
  L + B = 170 meters
  We need to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter wide boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The length of the outer boundary will be L + 2 meters (1 meter on each side).
  The breadth of the outer boundary will be B + 2 meters (1 meter on each side).
  The area of the outer boundary will be (L + 2) * (B + 2)
  The area of the rectangular plot will be L * B
  The area of the 1-meter wide boundary will be (L + 2) * (B + 2) - L * B
  The cost of gardening the 1-meter wide boundary will be 10 times the area of the boundary.
  Cost = 10 * [(L + 2) * (B + 2) - L * B]
       = 10 * [LB + 2L + 2B + 4 - LB]
       = 10 * [2L + 2B + 4]
       = 20L + 20B + 40
       = 20(L + B) + 40
       = 20(170) + 40
       = 3420
  Therefore, the cost of gardening the 1-meter wide boundary around the rectangular plot will be 3420.
  The answer is C: 3440.
Criticism:
  There is a minor error in the calculation in the last step. The correct answer should be 3420 instead of 3440.

Question: The capacity of a tank of dimensions (8 m × 6 m × 2.5 m) is
Choices:
  A: 120 litres
  B: 1200 litres
  C: 12000 litres
  D: 120000 litres
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a rectangular tank is given by the formula V = l × w × h, where l, w, and h are the length, width, and height of the tank, respectively.
Thought:
  The given dimensions of the tank are 8 m × 6 m × 2.5 m.
  Therefore, the volume of the tank is V = 8 × 6 × 2.5 = 120 cubic meters.
  1 cubic meter is equal to 1000 liters.
  Therefore, the capacity of the tank is 120 × 1000 = 120000 liters.
  The answer is D: 120000 litres.
Criticism:
  There is no flaw in the logic or reasoning used to arrive at the answer.
Action: Answer("D")

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 90 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Percentage gain is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) * 100.
  Cost Price is the price at which an item is purchased.
  Profit is the difference between the Selling Price and Cost Price.
  Selling Price is the price at which an item is sold.
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450.
  The merchant sold the oranges at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Thought: 
  The cost price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The selling price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50.
  The profit on 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50.
  The profit on 90 kg of oranges is Rs. 2.50 x 90 = Rs. 225.
  Percentage gain = (Profit/Cost Price) * 100 = (225/450) * 100 = 50%.
  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Percentage gain is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) * 100
  Profit is calculated as Selling Price - Cost Price
Thought: 
  Cost Price of 90 kg of oranges = Rs. 450
  Selling Price of 90 kg of oranges = 90 * Rs. 7.50 = Rs. 675
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price = Rs. 675 - Rs. 450 = Rs. 225
  Percentage gain = (Profit/Cost Price) * 100 = (225/450) * 100 = 50%
  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 92 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: There is well of depth 30m and frog is at bottom of the well. He jumps 3m up one day and falls back 2m down the same day. How many days will it take for the frog to come out of the well?
Choices:
  A: 25 days
  B: 26 days
  C: 27 days
  D: 28 days
  E: 29 days
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The well is of depth 30m.
  The frog jumps 3m up and falls back 2m down, so it covers a net distance of 1m per jump.
Thought:
  On the first day, the frog jumps up 3m and falls down 2m, so it covers a net distance of 1m.
  Therefore, on the first day, the frog reaches a height of 1m from the bottom of the well.
  On the second day, the frog jumps up 3m and falls down 2m, so it covers a net distance of 1m.
  Therefore, on the second day, the frog reaches a height of 2m from the bottom of the well.
  On the third day, the frog jumps up 3m and falls down 2m, so it covers a net distance of 1m.
  Therefore, on the third day, the frog reaches a height of 3m from the bottom of the well.
  In general, on the nth day, the frog reaches a height of (n-1)m from the bottom of the well.
  The frog needs to reach a height of 30m to come out of the well.
  Therefore, the frog will come out of the well on the 30th day.
  The answer is not listed among the choices.
  The closest answer is D: 28 days, which is incorrect.
  Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

  The frog jumps 3m up and falls back 2m down, so it climbs 1m every day.
  The well is 30m deep.
Thought: 
  The frog needs to climb 30m to get out of the well.
  The frog climbs 1m every day.
  Therefore, it will take the frog 30 days to climb out of the well.
  However, the frog doesn't need to climb the last 2m on the last day, because it will already be out of the well.
  So, it will take the frog 29 days to climb out of the well.

  On the first night, the frog falls 2m down and is now 27+2 = 25m from the top.
  On the second day, the frog jumps 3m up and is now 25-3 = 22m from the top.
  On the second night, the frog falls 2m down and is now 22+2 = 20m from the top.
  The frog jumps 3m up and falls 2m down each day. 
  Therefore, the frog climbs 1m each day.
  The frog needs to climb 30m to get out of the well.
  Therefore, it will take the frog 30/1 = 30 days to get out of the well.
  However, the frog has already climbed 3m on the first day.
  Therefore, it will take the frog 30-1 = 29 days to climb the remaining 27m.
Action: Answer("E")

Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume Joe's age = J, Joe's sister's age = S and Joe’s father's age = F.
  We know that J + S + F = 100.
Thought: 
  When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now.
  This means that the age difference between Joe and his sister will remain constant.
  So, let's assume that the age difference between Joe and his sister is X.
  So, when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister's age will be S + X, and Joe's age will be J + X.
  We also know that S + X = 2S, which means that X = S.
  Therefore, when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's age will be J + S, and his sister's age will be 2S.
  Now, we know that when Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father.
  Let's assume that when Joe's sister was as old as her father, her age was A.
  So, at that time, Joe's father's age was F - A, and Joe's sister's age was S - A.
  We know that F - A = 2(S - A).
  Therefore, F - A = 2S - 2A.
  We also know that J + S = F.
  So, substituting the value of S in the above equation, we get:
  F - A = 2(2S - J - A)
  F - A = 4S - 2J - 2A
  F = 4S - 2J + A
  We also know that J + S + F = 100.
  So, substituting the value of F in the above equation, we get:
  J + S + (4S - 2J + A) = 100
  3J + 5S + A = 100
  We have three variables and three equations. We can solve for them.
  From the equation S + X = 2S, we get X = S.
  Substituting the value of X in the equation J + S = F, we get J + S = F - S.
  So, F = 2S + J.
  Substituting the value of F in the equation 3J + 5S + A = 100, we get:

  3J + 5S
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the current age of Joe, his sister, and his father are x, y, and z respectively.
  The sum of their ages is 100, so x + y + z = 100.
Thought:
  When Joe is as old as his father, his father's age will increase by (z - x) years, and Joe's age will increase by (z - x) years.
  At that time, Joe's sister's age will be y + (z - x), which is twice her current age.
  So, we have the following equation: y + (z - x) = 2y
  Simplifying, we get: z - x = y
  Now, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father's age will be twice his sister's age when she was as old as her father.
  That means, (z - x) = 2(x - y)
  Simplifying, we get: z = 3x - 2y
  We also know that x + y + z = 100
  Substituting z = 3x - 2y, we get: x + y + 3x - 2y = 100
  Simplifying, we get: 4x - y = 100
  We have two equations: z = 3x - 2y and 4x - y = 100
  Solving these equations simultaneously, we get: x = 16, y = 12, and z = 72.
  Therefore, Joe's father is 72 years old.

Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Each time the coin lands on heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After flipping the coin 20 times, neither of them won or lost any amount.
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the coin landed on heads x times, and on tails y times.
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan each time the coin lands on heads, so he gave a total of 2x dollars.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher each time the coin lands on tails, so he gave a total of 3y dollars.
  Since neither of them won or lost any amount, we know that 2x = 3y.
  We also know that x + y = 20, since the coin was flipped 20 times.
  We can use these two equations to solve for x:
  2x = 3y
  x + y = 20
  Solving for y in the second equation, we get y = 20 - x.
  Substituting this into the first equation, we get 2x = 3(20 - x), which simplifies to 5x = 60.
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.
  Therefore, the coin landed on heads 12 times.
  The answer is E: 12.
Criticism: 
  There is no flaw in the logic and reasoning used to solve the problem.

  Multiplying the second equation by 2, we get 2x + 2y = 40.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Distance = Speed x Time
Thought:
  - Let's assume the distance between A and B is 'd'.
  - Let's assume Kevin took 't1' hours to reach B from A.
  - Therefore, he took 't1' hours to return from B to A as well.
  - Kevin drove at a constant speed of 70 mph from A to B. Therefore, d = 70t1.
  - On his way back from B to A, Kevin drove at a constant speed of 90 mph.
  - Let's assume he took 't2' hours to cover the distance between B and the point where he was 70 miles away from B.
  - Therefore, he took (t1 - t2 - 3) hours to cover the remaining distance between that point and A.
  - Distance covered in the first part of the journey = Distance covered in the second part of the journey + 70 miles.
  - Using the distance formula, we can write the equation as 70t1 = 90(t1 - t2 - 3) + d + 70.
  - Substituting d = 70t1, we get 70t1 = 90(t1 - t2 - 3) + 70t1 + 70.
  - Simplifying the equation, we get t1 - t2 = 10.
  - Using the distance formula, we can write d = 70t1.
  - Substituting t1 = t2 + 10, we get d = 70(t2 + 10).
  - We know that Kevin was 70 miles away from B exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip.
  - Therefore, he took (t1 - t2 - 3) hours to cover the remaining distance between that point and A.
  - Using the distance formula, we can write the equation as d - 70 = 90(t1 - t2 - 3).
  - Substituting d = 70(t2 + 10), we get 70(t2 + 10) - 70 = 90(t2 + 10 - t2 - 3).
  - Simplifying the equation, we get t2 = 4.
  - Substituting t2 = 4 in d = 70(t2 + 10), we get d = 420.
  - Therefore, the distance between A and B is 420 miles.
Answer: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The formula for distance is distance = rate x time.
  - The formula for time is time = distance / rate.
Thought:
  - Let's call the distance between A and B "d".
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to get from A to B "t".
  - Kevin's rate on the way to B is 70 mph, so we can write the equation d = 70t.
  - When Kevin turns around at B, he has traveled a distance of 2d (there and back).
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to get from B back to A "t2". We know that t2 is 3 hours less than the total time it takes Kevin to complete the trip.
  - We can write the equation 2d = 90t2.
  - We also know that when Kevin is 70 miles away from B, he has traveled a total of d + 70 miles. We can use this information to write another equation.
  - The time it takes Kevin to travel the first d miles is d/70, and the time it takes him to travel the next 70 miles is 70/90. The sum of these times is equal to the total time minus 3 hours, so we can write the equation d/70 + 70/90 = t - 3.
  - Now we have three equations with three variables (d, t, and t2). We can solve for d.
  - From the first equation, we know that t = d/70.
  - From the second equation, we know that t2 = 2d/90.
  - Substituting these values into the third equation, we get d/70 + 7/9 = 2d/90 - 3.
  - Simplifying this equation, we get d = 630.
  - Therefore, the distance between A and B is 630 miles.

  We know that the total duration of the trip is "t + t + 3 = 2t + 3" hours.
  We also know that the distance from B to A is "d" miles.
  Therefore, we can write the following equation:
    d - 70 = 90 * (2t + 3)
  We can simplify this equation to:
    d = 90 * (2t + 3) + 70
  We also know that the distance between A and B is the same as the distance between B and A, so:
    d = 90t + 70t

    160t = 90 * 2t + 220
    80t = 110
    t = 11/8 hours
  We can substitute this value of "t" into either equation to get:
    d = 90 * (2t + 3) + 70
    d = 90 * (2 * 11/8 + 3) + 70
    d = 270
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 270 miles.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the number of employees in the organization is "x".
  They want to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting an equal contribution from each employee.
  So, the contribution of each employee is 6 lakh/x.
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the total contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh.
  So, the new contribution of each employee is (6.24 lakh)/x.
Thought:
  The difference between the old contribution and the new contribution of each employee is Rs. 60.
  (6.24 lakh)/x - 6 lakh/x = 60
  Solving the above equation, we get x = 400.
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
  The answer is C: 400.
Criticism:
  There is no criticism to this answer.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  They have to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each employee.
  If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh.
  So, the difference between the two contribution amounts is Rs. 60n.
  We can set up two equations to solve for 'n'.
Thought:
  Let's assume that 'x' is the contribution of each employee.
  According to the question, the total contribution is Rs. 6 lakh.
  So, we can write the first equation as:
    nx = 600000
  Now, if each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the new contribution of each employee would be (x+60).
  According to the question, the new total contribution is Rs. 6.24 lakh.
  So, we can write the second equation as:
    n(x+60) = 624000
  We can solve these two equations to get the value of 'n'.
  From the first equation, we get:
    x = 600000/n
  Substituting this value of 'x' in the second equation, we get:
    n(600000/n + 60) = 624000
    600000 + 60n = 624000
    60n = 24000
    n = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
  The answer is C: 400.
Criticism:
  There is no criticism to this solution.
Action: Answer("C")

Knowledge:

  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then each employee would have contributed Rs. [(6.24 lakh - 6 lakh) / x] = Rs. (24000 / x) extra.
  The new contribution per employee would be Rs. [(6 lakh + 24000) / x] = Rs. (624000 / x).
Thought:
  According to the problem, the difference between the two contributions is Rs. 60 per employee.
  Therefore, we can set up an equation: (624000 / x) - (60000 / x) = 60
  Solving for x, we get x = 400.
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
  The answer is C: 400.
Criticism:
  There is no flaw in the logic or reasoning.

  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800

  There are 5 sons, 4 daughters, and 2 nephews.
  Each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew.
  Each son receives five times as much as each nephew.

  Then, each daughter receives 4x and each son receives 5x.

  Total amount = Rs 8600

Topic: Math
Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  To solve the problem, we need to use the formula:
  Actual value = (Incorrect value / correct value) * Incorrect value
Thought:
  Let's assume the actual number is x.
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number, so the incorrect value = (7/18)x.
  The student was supposed to find the value of 7/8 of the number, so the correct value = (7/8)x.
  According to the formula, we can write:
  x = [(7/18)x / (7/8)] * (7/18)x + 770
  Simplifying this equation, we get:
  x = 2520
  Therefore, the actual number is 2520.
  The answer is B: 2520.
Criticism: 
  There is no error in the solution.
Action: Answer("B")

  To solve the problem, we need to use the formula: 
  (error / correct answer) = (error / incorrect answer)
  We can then solve for the correct answer.

  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number, so his incorrect answer was (7/18)x.

  Solving for x, we get x = 2520
  Therefore, the number is 2520.

### Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 100 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile.
  The cab charges 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Thought:
  Let d be the maximum distance we can travel with $8.50.
  We can set up an equation to represent the cost of the trip: 
  $3.50 + $0.10(4n - 1) = $8.50, where n is the number of quarter-miles traveled after the first quarter-mile.
  Simplifying the equation, we have:
  $0.10(4n - 1) = $5.00
  4n - 1 = 50
  4n = 51
  n = 12.75
  Therefore, the total distance traveled is 1 + 12.75 = 13.75 miles.
  Thus, the maximum distance we can travel with $8.50 is 13.75 miles.
